class="nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-cGMI2b"><section class="DA9Qj nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-fmcmS-oXtfBe"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-c5RTEf"></div><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-qWD73c"><h5 class="cHE8Ub Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-qWD73c">Mandiant </h5><p class="nRhiJb-qJTHM khCp7b"></p></div></section></div></section><div class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-qWD73c-cGMI2b"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-ibL1re dzoHJ"></div><div class="OYL9D nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-OiUrBf" jsname="tx2NYc"><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Written by: Tyler McLellan, Brandan Schondorfer</p>
<hr></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>In September 2021, Mandiant discovered a post on exploit.in seeking partners for a new ransomware affiliate program. By October 21, 2021, the 54BB47h (Sabbath) ransomware shaming site and blog were created and quickly became the talk of security researchers. In contrast with most other affiliate programs, Mandiant observed two occasions where the ransomware operator provided its affiliates with pre-configured Cobalt Strike BEACON backdoor payloads. While the use of BEACON is common practice in ransomware intrusions, the use of a ransom affiliate program operator provided BEACON is unusual and offers both a challenge for attribution efforts while also offering additional avenues for detection.</p>
<p>Mandiant Advanced Practices began proactively identifying similar BEACON infrastructure across past Mandiant Consulting engagements, Advanced Practices external adversary discovery program, and commercially available malware repositories. Through this analysis, Advanced Practices linked the new Sabbath group to ransom activity under previously used names including Arcane and Eruption.</p>
<p>UNC2190, operating as Arcane and Sabbath, has targeted critical infrastructure including education, health, and natural resources in the United States and Canada since June 2021. The targeting of critical infrastructure by ransomware groups has become increasingly concerning as evidenced by governments moving to target ransomware actors as national security level threats with particular attention to groups that target and disrupt critical infrastructure.</p>
<h2>Stealthy Ransomware</h2>
<p>In July 2020, UNC2190 deployed ROLLCOAST ransomware while branded as Eruption. Mandiant has not observed samples of UNC2190-deployed ransomware in 2021 and no samples of ROLLCOAST have ever been submitted to VirusTotal. In the following sections, some of the technical reasons why UNC2190’s ransomware has evaded capture and discovery will be discussed.</p>
<h2>Next Level Extortion and ‘Backup Killers’</h2>
<p>Sabbath first came to light in October 2021 when the group publicly shamed and extorted a US school district on <a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/SecOpsDaily/comments/qfkpgc/the_new_ransomware_group_54bb47h_seem_to_have/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Reddit</a> and from a now suspended Twitter account, @54BB47h. During this recent extortion, the threat actor demanded a multi-million-dollar payment after deploying ransomware. Media reporting indicated that the group took the unusually aggressive step of emailing <a href="https://www.nbcdfw.com/news/local/howdy-hackers-email-parents-and-students-after-allen-isd-refuses-to-pay-ransom/2758256/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">staff, parents and even students</a> directly to further apply public pressure on the school district.</p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>@54BB47h on Twitter</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>UNC2190 uses a multifaceted extortion model where ransomware deployment may be quite limited in scope, bulk data is stolen as leverage, and the threat actor actively attempts to destroy backups.</p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Ransom note example</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>The threat actor has utilized public data leaks to extort the victims to pay ransom demands. While Sabbath operates a public shaming blog, Mandiant only observed victims being publicly extorted beginning in mid-November 2021, where 6 victims were added over the span of two days. Previously under the Arcane brand, Mandiant observed three victims publicly extorted in June 2021.</p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Source: Reddit SecOpsDaily</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2>Arcane Rebranded</h2>
<p>Mandiant discovered that the new Sabbath public shaming web portal and blog first published in October 2021 is nearly identical to that of Arcane from June 2021. This included the same text content, and minor changes to the name, color scheme, and logo. The threat actor kept consistent grammatical errors in their updated web forums.</p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Sabbath 54bb47h5qu4k7l4d7v5ix3i6ak6elysn3net4by4ihmvrhu7cvbskoqd.onion Website October 2021</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>thearcane.top website June 2021</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Behind the scenes, few technical changes were made to the affiliate model used to carry out the attacks between the rebranding from Arcane to Sabbath. BEACON samples and infrastructure from both ransomware affiliate services remained unchanged. The malware sample PE compile times were identical on Themida-packed BEACON droppers used by the threat actor (such as md5 6bd1a3849bb9d5f9ac5b4f4049081334 and 38667bc3ad2dcef35a5f343a5073e3f2).</p>
<h2>Hunting for UNC2190 BEACON Samples</h2>
<p>Since July 2020, UNC2190 has utilized <a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/defining-cobalt-strike-components" rel="noopener" target="_blank">BEACON</a> with unique Malleable profile elements, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>GET requests ending with kitten.gif, such as:
<ul>
<li>hxxps://markettc.biz/gifs/ZsoCzxU-X-5D3ZhV2zzKgc8SHhygCYmWpBRCS_mRV_SZxyWaaSPw7FFtcZ66twQ_uTDp5Edls<br>mRa6K8GPtMVBnKOHhM6EgcnE4znZPiyXskZJXmHLSYAnkpLwhOrxyCoRkFthelDg<br>VnuW7k3UVzDjEz3W4xuxSKBq2DuseaG-F0dob1M/kitten.gif</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>POST variable “image_url”, points to a specific image hosted on popular Russian social media site VK: hxxps://sun9-23.userapi.com/G4JvdZDEfLdIPlNN1-JkMGQ2unf2KEIV54Om5g/abJ70jGHfVk.jpg</li>
<li>User agent, such as: "Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/80.0.3987.163 Safari/537.36"</li>
</ul>
<p>Mandiant discovered additional infrastructure similarities utilized by UNC2190 including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Actual IPs masked using a cloud service.</li>
<li>Self-signed TLS certificate common name “Microsoft IT TLS CA 5”</li>
</ul>
<h2>Evolving to Evade Antivirus Detection</h2>
<p>In March 2021, Mandiant Consulting observed an intrusion for another tracked UNC group where antivirus had detected and blocked two attempts to load a BEACON payload which Mandiant attributes to UNC2190. Subsequently, a different tracked threat actor deployed different ransomware at this victim with more success. Starting July 6, 2021, Mandiant detected the use of Themida to pack UNC2190 BEACON malware and protect it from detection.</p>
<h2>ROLLCOAST Ransomware Deep Dive</h2>
<p>In July 2020, Mandiant first detected ROLLCOAST ransomware usage by UNC2190. ROLLCOAST</p>
<p>is a ransomware program that encrypts files on logical drives attached to a system. ROLLCOAST is a Dynamic Linked Library (DLL) with no named exports. When observed by Mandiant it uniquely had only one ordinal export 0x01. This suggested the sample was designed to avoid detection and be invoked within memory, possibly through BEACON provided to affiliates. Incident responders working on similar intrusions should capture memory for analysis. ROLLCOAST was not written to disk during this intrusion and was only detected in memory by Mandiant.</p>
<p>The malware begins by checking the system language and exits if it detects a non-supported language code from the table below. Many other ransomware families have similar checks to avoid encrypting systems in Russia and other Commonwealth of Independent States member countries presumably to avoid attracting the attention of law enforcement in countries where the ransomware operator and affiliates are more likely to reside.</p>
<h2>Language Exclusions</h2>

<h2>Similarities to Tycoon</h2>
<p>Mandiant compared elements of ROLLCOAST to elements of <a href="https://blogs.blackberry.com/en/2020/06/threat-spotlight-tycoon-ransomware-targets-education-and-software-sectors" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Tycoon ransomware</a> and found some similarities:</p>
<ul>
<li>Both ransomware families encrypt files using AES in GCM mode</li>
<li>Overlap between the ignored directories, files, and extensions including the ignored extension “.lolz”.</li>
</ul>
<p>This suggests the developers modelled ROLLCOAST on, or copied elements from, Tycoon ransomware. ROLLCOAST and TYCOON differ in their overall implementations: TYCOON is a Java based ransomware whereas ROLLCOAST is not. In addition, there is functionality in the publicly reported TYCOON that ROLLCOAST does not appear to have (shell commands, backup tampering, firewall tampering, wmic).</p>
<h2>ROLLCOAST Strings</h2>
<pre><code>FOUND DEVICE:
Start encryption of %s
[-] Failed to init dir traverse for: %s
Finished encryption of %s
Work out other countries. Don't be fool!
Hello from test.dll. Parameter is '%s'
Hello from test.dll. There is no parameter
Microsoft Primitive Provider
[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_NOT_FOUND
[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_INVALID_PARAMETER
[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_NO_MEMORY
[-] AES FAILED 1: UNDEFINED
ChainingModeGCM</code></pre>
<h2>ROLLCOAST Encrypted File Naming Convention</h2>
<p>Files are encrypted and renamed to this format: .[].</p>
<p>Example encrypted file recovered from VirusTotal:</p>
<p>covid results from .pdf.[6EEC0F355072].54bb47h</p>
<h2>Conclusion</h2>
<p>Although UNC2190 is a lesser known and potentially a smaller ransomware affiliate group, it’s smaller size and repeated rebranding has allowed it to avoid much public scrutiny. In Mandiant’s 2021 Trends and 2022 Predictions report, ransomware data theft operations affecting healthcare are noted as having increased from January 2020 to June 2021, despite some groups claiming they would avoid targeting hospitals. UNC2190 has continued to operate over the past year while making only minor changes to their strategies and tooling, including the introduction of a commercial packer and the rebranding of their service offering. This highlights how well-known tools, such as BEACON, can lead to impactful and lucrative incidents even when leveraged by lesser-known groups.</p>

<p><em>Note: FE_Hunting rules are designed to broadly capture suspicious files and are not designed to detect a particular malware or threat.</em></p>
<p> </p>
<pre><code>rule FE_Hunting_THEMIDA_strings_FEBeta
{
    meta:
        author = &quot;Mandiant&quot;
        date_created = &quot;2021-10-26&quot;
        date_modified = &quot;2021-10-26&quot;
        md5 = &quot;7669f00b467e2990be182584b341c0e8&quot;
        rev = 2
        sid = 415583
    strings:
        $themida = &quot;.themida&quot; nocase
    condition:
        uint16(0) == 0x5A4D and filesize &lt; 20MB and (@themida[1] &lt; 1024)
}</code></pre>

Again"],null,null,[[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eWritten by: Tyler McLellan, Brandan Schondorfer\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eIn September 2021, Mandiant discovered a post on exploit.in seeking partners for a new ransomware affiliate program. By October 21, 2021, the 54BB47h (Sabbath) ransomware shaming site and blog were created and quickly became the talk of security researchers. In contrast with most other affiliate programs, Mandiant observed two occasions where the ransomware operator provided its affiliates with pre-configured Cobalt Strike BEACON backdoor payloads. While the use of BEACON is common practice in ransomware intrusions, the use of a ransom affiliate program operator provided BEACON is unusual and offers both a challenge for attribution efforts while also offering additional avenues for detection.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMandiant Advanced Practices began proactively identifying similar BEACON infrastructure across past Mandiant Consulting engagements, Advanced Practices external adversary discovery program, and commercially available malware repositories. Through this analysis, Advanced Practices linked the new Sabbath group to ransom activity under previously used names including Arcane and Eruption.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUNC2190, operating as Arcane and Sabbath, has targeted critical infrastructure including education, health, and natural resources in the United States and Canada since June 2021. The targeting of critical infrastructure by ransomware groups has become increasingly concerning as evidenced by governments moving to target ransomware actors as national security level threats with particular attention to groups that target and disrupt critical infrastructure.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eStealthy Ransomware\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn July 2020, UNC2190 deployed ROLLCOAST ransomware while branded as Eruption. Mandiant has not observed samples of UNC2190-deployed ransomware in 2021 and no samples of ROLLCOAST have ever been submitted to VirusTotal. In the following sections, some of the technical reasons why UNC2190’s ransomware has evaded capture and discovery will be discussed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eNext Level Extortion and ‘Backup Killers’\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSabbath first came to light in October 2021 when the group publicly shamed and extorted a US school district on \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.reddit.com/r/SecOpsDaily/comments/qfkpgc/the_new_ransomware_group_54bb47h_seem_to_have/\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eReddit\u003c/a\u003e and from a now suspended Twitter account, @54BB47h. During this recent extortion, the threat actor demanded a multi-million-dollar payment after deploying ransomware. Media reporting indicated that the group took the unusually aggressive step of emailing \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.nbcdfw.com/news/local/howdy-hackers-email-parents-and-students-after-allen-isd-refuses-to-pay-ransom/2758256/\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003estaff, parents and even students\u003c/a\u003e directly to further apply public pressure on the school district.\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003e@54BB47h on Twitter\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten1_nesk.max-1000x1000.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eUNC2190 uses a multifaceted extortion model where ransomware deployment may be quite limited in scope, bulk data is stolen as leverage, and the threat actor actively attempts to destroy backups.\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eRansom note example\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1100x1100.png 1060w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png 1502w"," 1060px,  1502px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten2_crme.max-1600x1600.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eThe threat actor has utilized public data leaks to extort the victims to pay ransom demands. While Sabbath operates a public shaming blog, Mandiant only observed victims being publicly extorted beginning in mid-November 2021, where 6 victims were added over the span of two days. Previously under the Arcane brand, Mandiant observed three victims publicly extorted in June 2021.\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eSource: Reddit SecOpsDaily\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten3_yadh.max-1000x1000.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003ch2\u003eArcane Rebranded\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMandiant discovered that the new Sabbath public shaming web portal and blog first published in October 2021 is nearly identical to that of Arcane from June 2021. This included the same text content, and minor changes to the name, color scheme, and logo. The threat actor kept consistent grammatical errors in their updated web forums.\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eSabbath 54bb47h5qu4k7l4d7v5ix3i6ak6elysn3net4by4ihmvrhu7cvbskoqd.onion Website October 2021\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten4_itkg.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003ethearcane.top website June 2021\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/kitten5_yaix.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eBehind the scenes, few technical changes were made to the affiliate model used to carry out the attacks between the rebranding from Arcane to Sabbath. BEACON samples and infrastructure from both ransomware affiliate services remained unchanged. The malware sample PE compile times were identical on Themida-packed BEACON droppers used by the threat actor (such as md5 6bd1a3849bb9d5f9ac5b4f4049081334 and 38667bc3ad2dcef35a5f343a5073e3f2).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eHunting for UNC2190 BEACON Samples\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSince July 2020, UNC2190 has utilized \u003ca href\u003d\"https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/defining-cobalt-strike-components\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eBEACON\u003c/a\u003e with unique Malleable profile elements, including:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eGET requests ending with kitten.gif, such as:\r\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ehxxps://markettc.biz/gifs/ZsoCzxU-X-5D3ZhV2zzKgc8SHhygCYmWpBRCS_mRV_SZxyWaaSPw7FFtcZ66twQ_uTDp5Edls\u003cbr\u003emRa6K8GPtMVBnKOHhM6EgcnE4znZPiyXskZJXmHLSYAnkpLwhOrxyCoRkFthelDg\u003cbr\u003eVnuW7k3UVzDjEz3W4xuxSKBq2DuseaG-F0dob1M/kitten.gif\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePOST variable “image_url”, points to a specific image hosted on popular Russian social media site VK: hxxps://sun9-23.userapi.com/G4JvdZDEfLdIPlNN1-JkMGQ2unf2KEIV54Om5g/abJ70jGHfVk.jpg\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eUser agent, such as: \"Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/80.0.3987.163 Safari/537.36\"\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMandiant discovered additional infrastructure similarities utilized by UNC2190 including:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eActual IPs masked using a cloud service.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSelf-signed TLS certificate common name “Microsoft IT TLS CA 5”\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eEvolving to Evade Antivirus Detection\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn March 2021, Mandiant Consulting observed an intrusion for another tracked UNC group where antivirus had detected and blocked two attempts to load a BEACON payload which Mandiant attributes to UNC2190. Subsequently, a different tracked threat actor deployed different ransomware at this victim with more success. Starting July 6, 2021, Mandiant detected the use of Themida to pack UNC2190 BEACON malware and protect it from detection.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eROLLCOAST Ransomware Deep Dive\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn July 2020, Mandiant first detected ROLLCOAST ransomware usage by UNC2190. ROLLCOAST\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eis a ransomware program that encrypts files on logical drives attached to a system. ROLLCOAST is a Dynamic Linked Library (DLL) with no named exports. When observed by Mandiant it uniquely had only one ordinal export 0x01. This suggested the sample was designed to avoid detection and be invoked within memory, possibly through BEACON provided to affiliates. Incident responders working on similar intrusions should capture memory for analysis. ROLLCOAST was not written to disk during this intrusion and was only detected in memory by Mandiant.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe malware begins by checking the system language and exits if it detects a non-supported language code from the table below. Many other ransomware families have similar checks to avoid encrypting systems in Russia and other Commonwealth of Independent States member countries presumably to avoid attracting the attention of law enforcement in countries where the ransomware operator and affiliates are more likely to reside.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLanguage Exclusions\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eROLLCOAST will exit if the system language matches one of the following:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv style\u003d\"color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%\"\u003e\n\u003cdiv style\u003d\"border:1px solid #000000;padding:16px\"\u003eUzbek (Latin, Uzbekistan)\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd style\u003d\"border:1px solid #000000;padding:16px\"\u003e0x444\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd style\u003d\"border:1px solid #000000;padding:16px\"\u003eTatar (Russia)\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eSimilarities to Tycoon\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMandiant compared elements of ROLLCOAST to elements of \u003ca href\u003d\"https://blogs.blackberry.com/en/2020/06/threat-spotlight-tycoon-ransomware-targets-education-and-software-sectors\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eTycoon ransomware\u003c/a\u003e and found some similarities:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eBoth ransomware families encrypt files using AES in GCM mode\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOverlap between the ignored directories, files, and extensions including the ignored extension “.lolz”.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis suggests the developers modelled ROLLCOAST on, or copied elements from, Tycoon ransomware. ROLLCOAST and TYCOON differ in their overall implementations: TYCOON is a Java based ransomware whereas ROLLCOAST is not. In addition, there is functionality in the publicly reported TYCOON that ROLLCOAST does not appear to have (shell commands, backup tampering, firewall tampering, wmic).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eROLLCOAST Strings\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode\u003eFOUND DEVICE:\r\nStart encryption of %s\r\n[-] Failed to init dir traverse for: %s\r\nFinished encryption of %s\r\nWork out other countries. Don't be fool!\r\nHello from test.dll. Parameter is '%s'\r\nHello from test.dll. There is no parameter\r\nMicrosoft Primitive Provider\r\n[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_NOT_FOUND\r\n[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_INVALID_PARAMETER\r\n[-] AES FAILED 1: STATUS_NO_MEMORY\r\n[-] AES FAILED 1: UNDEFINED\r\nChainingModeGCM\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eROLLCOAST Encrypted File Naming Convention\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFiles are encrypted and renamed to this format: .[].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eExample encrypted file recovered from VirusTotal:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ecovid results from .pdf.[6EEC0F355072].54bb47h\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eConclusion\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlthough UNC2190 is a lesser known and potentially a smaller ransomware affiliate group, it’s smaller size and repeated rebranding has allowed it to avoid much public scrutiny. In Mandiant’s 2021 Trends and 2022 Predictions report, ransomware data theft operations affecting healthcare are noted as having increased from January 2020 to June 2021, despite some groups claiming they would avoid targeting hospitals. UNC2190 has continued to operate over the past year while making only minor changes to their strategies and tooling, including the introduction of a commercial packer and the rebranding of their service offering. This highlights how well-known tools, such as BEACON, can lead to impactful and lucrative incidents even when leveraged by lesser-known groups.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eAcknowledgements\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWith thanks Joshua Shilko for analytical contributions, Barry Vengerik, Tufail Ahmed, Isif Ibrahima, Andrew Thompson,
